The Dream Warning on Studying Sanusi's Creed
Bajuri narrates two dreams emphasizing the necessity of studying Sanusi's creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how dream narratives were used to stress the necessity of studying a specific creed (aqidah) and the theological reasoning behind the punishment described.

Core Idea
Dreams can reveal the grave importance of learning correct creed.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary presents two remarkable dream stories that underscore the importance of studying Sanusi's creed. The first dream involves a deceased scholar being questioned by the angels, who rebuke him for not having studied this specific creed. The second dream shows Prophet Ibrahim teaching the same creed to children in Paradise. These accounts are not mere tales; they carry a serious lesson about the necessity of sound theological education.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the story unfold naturally before analyzing it.
Notice the emotional tone: the angels speak with anger and threat.
2
Understand the objection and answer
The author anticipates a potential objection: if reading a specific creed is permissible, why punishment? Follow the answer carefully.
The key is that the punishment may stem from hidden internal faults like belittlement.
3
Reflect on the second dream
The second dream shows Prophet Ibrahim teaching Sanusi's creed in Paradise. Consider what this suggests about the creed's status.
Al-Zawawi notes it may be the 'small creed' (al-ʿAqīda al-Ṣughrā).
4
Connect to broader lesson
Ask yourself: Why would scholars use dreams to motivate study? What does this tell us about the importance of creedal precision?
These stories serve as both warning and encouragement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكى فيه عن السنوسي: أنه حُكِي له أن صاحبه محمد بن يحيى رأى صاحباً له من أهل العلم بعد موته، فسأله عما لَقِيَهُ من منكر ونكير، فقال: سألاني عن ديني وعما قرأتُ من كتب التوحيد، فقلت: قرأتُ عقيدةَ فلانٍ وعقيدةَ فلان، فقالا بغضب وتهديد: ولأي شيء لم تقرأ عقيدة السنوسي؟ فقال: قرأتُ غيرها من العقائد. فقالا: وهلا قرأتها، لو قرأتها لكفتك عن غيرها، وضرباه بمَقْمَعٍ من حديد ضربتين أو ثلاثاً، وإنما كان الضربُ والعتاب لعدم قراءتي لها مع أني كنتُ أعرِفُ التوحيد بالبراهين القطعية، فكيف حال المقلّد والجاهل ؟ فإن قلت: لا عِقَابَ على المباح؟ أجيب بأن غالب المصائب من الأمراض الباطنة، فلعله انضم إلى عدم قراءتها أمر باطني كتنقيص أو اعتراض؛ لأن المعاصَرَةَ حرمان، وتركه اسم الميت ستراً عليه. وحكي أيضاً أن بعض الصالحين رؤي في المنام بعد موته فقيل له: ما فعل الله بك؟ فقال: أدخلني الجنة ورأيتُ سيدنا إبراهيم الخليل يُقْرِئُ عقيدة سيدي محمد السنوسي الصبيان، وهم يقرؤونها في الألواح ، ويجهرون بقراءتها، قال الزَّوَاوِيُّ: وأظنه قال: العقيدةَ الصغرى. أفاده بعض شراح المتن مع زيادة.
And he related in it from al-Sanusi: that it was narrated to him that his companion Muhammad ibn Yahya saw a companion of his from the people of knowledge after his death, and he asked him about what he encountered from Munkar and Nakir. He said: 'They asked me about my religion and what I had read from books of tawhid. I said: I read the creed of so-and-so and the creed of so-and-so. They said angrily and threateningly: Why did you not read the creed of al-Sanusi? He said: I read other creeds. They said: Why did you not read it? Had you read it, it would have sufficed you from others. And they struck him with a mace of iron two or three blows. And the striking and rebuke was only because of my not reading it, even though I knew tawhid with decisive proofs. So how is the case of the muqallid and the ignorant?' If you say: There is no punishment for what is permissible? The answer is that most afflictions are from internal diseases. Perhaps there was added to his not reading it an internal matter such as belittlement or objection, because contemporaneity (with the author) is deprivation. And he omitted the name of the deceased to protect him. And it was also narrated that a certain righteous person was seen in a dream after his death and it was said to him: What did Allah do with you? He said: He entered me into Paradise and I saw our master Ibrahim al-Khalil teaching the creed of my master Muhammad al-Sanusi to children, and they were reading it on tablets and reciting it aloud. Al-Zawawi said: I think he said: the small creed. This was related by some commentators of the matn with an addition.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage narrates two dreams about the importance of studying Sanusi's creed. In the first dream, a deceased scholar is questioned by the angels Munkar and Nakir. They rebuke him for not having read Sanusi's creed despite knowing tawhid through proofs, and they strike him. The questioner might object that reading a specific creed is not obligatory, so punishment is unjust. The answer is that the affliction may result from an internal fault like belittlement. The second dream shows Prophet Ibrahim teaching Sanusi's creed to children in Paradise, indicating its high station. The passage ends with a note that al-Zawawi thinks the 'small creed' is meant.

Key Terms
عقيدة السنوسي
منكر ونكير
مقلد
تقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dream implies that other creeds are invalid or that reading Sanusi's creed is obligatory for salvation.
Correction: The text does not declare other creeds invalid; rather, the punishment is linked to a possible internal fault (belittlement) despite the man's knowledge, and the second dream shows the creed's high status but not exclusivity.

Checkpoint
According to the first dream, why was the deceased scholar punished despite knowing tawhid with decisive proofs?
A) Because he did not act on his knowledge
B) Because he did not read Sanusi's creed
C) Because he denied the angels
D) Because he taught falsehood

Key Takeaway
Dream narratives served as powerful motivators to study authoritative creeds like al-Sanusi's, warning that neglect could reflect hidden faults even in knowledgeable individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a particular work of a scholar simply because you didn't know its importance, or because it seemed 'too simple' or 'too detailed'? What internal disease—like arrogance, laziness, or pride in your own learning—might have caused you to overlook it? Will you commit to examining your heart and seeking out what you have neglected?
?
The deceased scholar knew tawhid with decisive proofs, yet was punished for not studying al-Sanusi's creed. What does this tell you about the hidden faults in your own heart? Are you relying on your knowledge while secretly looking down on a specific teaching or scholar? If you were asked in the grave, could you name a specific creed you have studied, or would you be struck for your neglect?
?
The second dream shows Prophet Ibrahim teaching al-Sanusi's creed to children in Paradise. Imagine your own afterlife: will you be among those who taught or learned this creed, or will you be among those who ignored it out of pride or indifference? What concrete step will you take today to study a text of correct creed thoroughly, not just casually?

Beginning Matters with God's Name
Presentation of two hadiths on beginning matters with basmala and hamdala, with variant readings and explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and significance of the hadiths about beginning important matters with basmala and hamdala, and the implications of the terms abtar, aqta', ajdham.

Core Idea
Actions begun without God's name or praise are deficient in blessing, even if outwardly complete.

This lesson presents two well-known hadiths that encourage beginning important matters with the basmala or the hamdala. The hadiths use three synonymous terms to describe the outcome of neglecting this practice: abtar, aqta', and ajdham. We will explore what these terms mean and why the practice is emphasized in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the two hadiths: one about beginning with basmala, the other with hamdala. Observe the three variant endings for each.
The variants are: abtar, aqta', ajdham.
2
Understand the common meaning
The commentary states that all three terms essentially mean the matter is deficient and of little blessing, even if it appears complete externally.
The deficiency is in spiritual blessing, not physical completion.
3
Clarify the scope of 'amr'
The passage explains that 'amr' here means 'thing' or 'affair', not the opposite of prohibition. It refers to any important matter.
'Dhi bal' means 'of importance'.
4
Reflect on application
Consider why beginning with God's name or praise is emphasized for actions like eating, writing, or public speaking. How does this lesson affect your daily practice?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كُلُّ أَمْرِ ذِي بَالِ لَا يُبْدَأُ فِيهِ ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم فَهُوَ أَبْتَرُ»، وفي رواية: «فَهُوَ أَقْطَعُ»، وفي رواية: «فَهُوَ أَجْذَمُ»). والمعنى على كلّ : أنه ناقص وقليل البركة، فهو وإن تَمَّ حِسّاً؛ لا يتم معنى مع خبرِ : كُلُّ أَمْرٍ ذِي بَالِ لَا يُبْدَأُ فِيهِ بِالْحَمْدُ اللَّهِ فَهُوَ أبْتَرُ»، وفي رواية: «فَهُوَ أَقْطَعُ»، وفي رواية: «فَهُوَ أَجْدَمُ، والمعنى على كل: أنه ناقص وقليل البركة كما تقدم. والمراد بالأمر في هذين الخبرين الشيء، لا ضد النهي، فهو واحد الأمور. وقوله: ذي) بال أي.
Every important matter in which one does not begin with 'In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful' is curtailed (abtar), and in another narration: 'it is cut off (aqta'')', and in another narration: 'it is maimed (ajdham)'. And the meaning in all is that it is deficient and of little blessing; even if it is complete sensibly, it is not complete in meaning... with the report: 'Every important matter in which one does not begin with 'Praise be to God' is curtailed', and in another narration: 'it is cut off', and in another narration: 'it is maimed', and the meaning in all is that it is deficient and of little blessing as previously mentioned. And what is meant by 'matter' (amr) in these two reports is 'thing' (shay'), not the opposite of prohibition, so it is one of the things. And his saying: 'dhi bal' means: of importance.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents two hadiths about the importance of beginning actions with God's name (basmala) or praise (hamdala). It first gives the wording of the basmala hadith with three variant endings: abtar, aqta', ajdham. It then states the common meaning: such an action is deficient and lacks blessing, even if externally complete. It then mentions a similar hadith about beginning with al-hamdulillah (praise), again with the same three variant terms, and repeats the meaning. The author clarifies that the word 'amr' here means 'thing' or 'affair', not the technical term 'command'. Finally, it explains that 'dhi bal' means 'of importance' or 'matter of concern'.

Key Terms
أبتر
أقطع
أجذم
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله
ذي بال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the hadith means the action is completely invalid or sinful if not begun with basmala or hamdala.
Correction: The hadith actually indicates that such actions are deficient in blessing, not that they are invalid or sinful. The terms abtar, aqta', ajdham all point to a lack of completeness and blessing, not outright invalidity.

Checkpoint
What do the words 'abtar', 'aqta'', and 'ajdham' all indicate according to the commentary?
A) The matter is invalid and sinful.
B) The matter is deficient and of little blessing.
C) The matter is successful and blessed.
D) The matter is merely disliked.

Key Takeaway
Beginning important matters with God's name or praise brings blessing and completeness; neglecting this leads to spiritual deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an important conversation or task you began recently without consciously saying 'Bismillah' or 'Alhamdulillah'. Did you sense any lack of blessing or incompleteness in its outcome? How might that moment have been different if you had begun with God's name?
?
You often say 'Bismillah' before eating, but do you truly believe that without it the meal is deficient in blessing – even if you are full? How does that truth challenge your daily rituals?
?
The hadith says 'every important matter' – what matters in your life do you habitually forget to begin with God's name or praise? Will you commit today to changing one of those and observe the difference?

Rulings on Saying Basmalah Before Acts
Al-Bajuri enumerates opinions on basmalah before prohibited/disliked acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly opinions on saying Bismillah before prohibited and disliked acts, and the reasoning behind the preponderant view.

Core Idea
Saying Bismillah before a prohibited act is defiance; the ruling depends on the act's essence.

Al-Bajuri presents a nuanced debate: should we say Bismillah before acts that Allah has forbidden? Scholars differ based on whether the prohibition is by essence or by circumstance. This lesson explores these opinions and their underlying logic, inviting careful reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the entire Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the list of opinions introduced by 'قيل'.
The passage begins with a note about the fā' (فَتَحْرُمُ) being explanatory.
2
Identify the four opinions
The passage presents four opinions on saying basmalah before prohibited and disliked acts. List them: 1) disliked on both, 2) forbidden on both, 3) disliked on disliked and forbidden on prohibited absolutely, 4) the preponderant: disliked on disliked by essence and forbidden on prohibited by essence.
Note that each opinion involves the concept of murāghamah (defiance).
3
Understand the preponderant opinion
Focus on the fourth opinion: the ruling depends on whether the act's prohibition is by essence (li-dhātihi) or by circumstance (li-‘āriḍ). Only when by essence is there defiance, so basmalah is forbidden/prohibited accordingly.
If prohibition is due to circumstance, the act itself is receptive to blessing, so basmalah is not forbidden.
4
Consider the derived ruling on necessity
The passage adds that even if necessity makes a prohibited act permissible (e.g., eating carrion), basmalah remains prohibited because the essence is unreceptive. Reflect on why necessity does not apply to the basmalah itself.
The author ends with 'fata'ammal' (so reflect), inviting you to ponder the implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: فَتَحْرُمُ عَلَى الْمُحَرَّم... إلخ) لا يتفرّعُ على ما قبله، فلعل الفاء فاء الفصيحة. ثم إن هذا أحد أقوال، حاصلها أنه قيل تُكْرَهُ التسمية على كلّ من المكروه والمحرّم ولو لعارض؛ لما في ذلك من مراغَمَةِ الشارع بجعل المنهي عنه محلاً للبركة. وقيل: تحرم التسمية عليهما؛ إذ المراغمة تقتضي التحريم، بل قال بعضهم: إن التسمية على شُرب الخمر كُفْرٌ. ولا يخفى أن كلّاً من أصحاب القولين يقول بتفاوتِ ما قال به من الكراهة أو الحُرْمَة. وقيل : تُكْرَهُ على المكروه، وتَحْرُمُ على المحرَّم مطلقاً. وقيل - وهو الراجح -: تُكْرَهُ على المكروه لذاته، وتَحْرُمُ على المحرَّم لذاته؛ إذ المراغمة إنما تتحقق حينئذ، دون ما إذا كانا لعارض؛ لأن العارِضَ إنما يتسبب عنه مَنْعُ الاستعمال فقط، ولا يمنع التسمية؛ إذ المحل في ذاته قابل لها، فلا مراغَمَةَ. كذا في حواشي البهجة" نقلاً عن "العباب" وغيره.
عنه لذاته،
وأخذ من هذا بعض المحققين من أشياخنا أنه لو عَرَضَ الإباحةُ لما نُهِيَ كأن اضطر لأكل الميتة أو شُرْبِ جَرْعَةِ حَمرٍ لإساعة ما غَصَّ به مَنْ يريد الأَدَم سِوَى البصل النيء؛ تَبْقَى التسمية على الامتناع؛ إذ المحل في ذاته غيرُ قابِل لها، والضرورة لا مَدْخَلَ لها في التسمية. فتدبر.)
(His saying: 'So it is forbidden upon the prohibited... etc.') It does not branch from what precedes it; perhaps the fā' is the fā' of rhetorical explanation (al-fā' al-faṣīḥah). Then indeed this is one of several opinions. Their summary: it is said that saying basmalah is disliked (yukrahu) upon both the disliked and the prohibited, even if by circumstance, because of the defiance (murāghamah) of the Lawgiver by making that which is prohibited a locus for blessing. And it is said: saying basmalah is forbidden upon them both, since defiance necessitates prohibition; rather some said that saying basmalah upon drinking wine is unbelief (kufr). It is not hidden that each of the holders of the two opinions speaks of the gradation of what he said of dislikedness or unlawfulness. And it is said: it is disliked upon the disliked and forbidden upon the prohibited absolutely. And it is said – and it is the preponderant opinion (al-rājiḥ): it is disliked upon the disliked by essence, and forbidden upon the prohibited by essence; for defiance (murāghamah) is only realized then, not when both are by circumstance, because circumstance only brings about the prevention of usage (man' al-isti'māl) and does not prevent saying basmalah, since the locus (al-maḥall) in its essence is receptive to it, so there is no defiance. Thus in the glosses of 'al-Bahjah' quoting from 'al-‘Ubāb' and others.
Concerning it [i.e., the prohibited] by essence,
And some verifying scholars among our shaykhs derived from this that if permissibility were to occur for that which is prohibited – such as being forced to eat carrion or drink a gulp of wine to quench choking except for raw onion – the basmalah remains prohibited; because the locus in its essence is not receptive to it, and necessity has no entry in basmalah. So reflect.)
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the differing opinions among scholars regarding the ruling on saying the basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) before performing acts that are either prohibited or disliked. The author begins by noting that this discussion does not branch from the previous definitions; the fā' (so) is the fā' of rhetorical explanation (al-fā' al-faṣīḥah). He then summarizes the views. First view: saying basmalah is disliked (makrūh) before both prohibited and disliked acts, even if by circumstance, because it involves defiance (murāghamah) of the Lawgiver by invoking blessing on something He prohibited. Second view: it is forbidden (ḥarām), because defiance implies prohibition; some even said that saying basmalah on wine is kufr. Both views acknowledge gradation (tafāwut) in the intensity of hatred or unlawfulness. Third view: it is disliked on the disliked and forbidden on the prohibited absolutely. Fourth view – which is the preponderant (al-rājiḥ): it is disliked on the disliked by essence and forbidden on the prohibited by essence. The reasoning is that defiance is only realized when the act is inherently prohibited or disliked, not when the ruling is due to an external circumstance. With circumstantial rulings, the circumstance only prevents using the act, but does not prevent saying basmalah because the locus (the act itself) is receptive to blessing. Thus there is no defiance. The passage then adds a derived ruling from some verifying scholars: if an act that is prohibited by essence becomes permissible due to necessity (e.g., eating carrion when starving), still saying basmalah upon it is prohibited, because the essence of the act remains unreceptive to blessing, and necessity does not affect the ruling of basmalah. The author ends with 'fata'ammal' (so reflect), inviting careful thought.

Key Terms
التسمية
المُرَاغَمَة
الراجح
المحل
العارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if an act becomes permissible due to necessity (like eating carrion when starving), saying basmalah upon it becomes permissible.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the ruling on basmalah is based on the act's essence, not its permissibility. Since the essence remains unreceptive, basmalah remains prohibited even when the act is allowed by necessity.

Checkpoint
What is the preponderant opinion (al-rājiḥ) regarding saying basmalah before acts that are prohibited or disliked?
A) It is disliked before all prohibited and disliked acts.
B) It is forbidden before all prohibited and disliked acts.
C) It is disliked before disliked by essence and forbidden before prohibited by essence.
D) It is disliked before the disliked and forbidden before the prohibited absolutely.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on saying Basmalah before an act depends on whether the act's prohibition is by essence or by circumstance; only essential prohibition necessitates forbidding Basmalah, and necessity does not change this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever said 'Bismillah' before doing something you knew was wrong, hoping that blessing it would make it acceptable? What does this lesson reveal about the weight of that action and your relationship with God's commands?
?
Think of an act you sometimes do that is disliked or prohibited but you justify it by circumstances. Does this teaching change how you approach that act? Will you commit to never invoking God's name on things He essentially forbids, even when circumstances seem to allow the act itself?
?
The derived ruling teaches that even when necessity makes a prohibited act permissible, basmalah remains prohibited because the essence is unreceptive. How does this challenge your tendency to combine convenience with spirituality? Will you now be more careful to distinguish between the act and the blessing upon it?

Conditions for Basmalah and Resolving an Objection
Al-Bajuri explains conditions for basmalah and resolves an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conditions under which saying basmalah before an act is recommended (mustaḥabb) and how an apparent contradiction between two reports is resolved.

Core Idea
Basmalah is not sought for acts with prescribed beginnings or that are inherently good.

In this passage, al-Bajuri continues his commentary on Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin, clarifying the precise conditions for the basmalah to be prescribed before an act. He discusses the 'third type' of acts, the role of the Lawgiver's specification, and then addresses an objection that two reports about basmalah for prayer seem to contradict each other. The lesson shows how fiqh methodology resolves apparent textual conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third type
Read the first line: 'And it is not sought upon the third type – like wearing sandals.' Understand that this refers to acts that are neither recommended nor prohibited in essence, and for which basmalah is not prescribed; rather, it is better to omit it out of reverence.
The third type excludes acts that are inherently prohibited or disliked, and also acts that are purely dhikr or trivial.
2
Understand the condition about beginning
Examine the condition: 'And that the Lawgiver does not make for it a beginning other than basmalah and ḥamdalah...' This means if the act has a prescribed opening (like takbir in prayer), basmalah is not sought before it.
The condition covers two scenarios: no prescribed beginning, or basmalah itself as the beginning. The first scenario is not intended here.
3
Analyze the objection and its resolution
The text mentions an objection: the two reports (one commanding basmalah before prayer, the other not) seem contradictory. The resolution is based on different narrations (raf' of the dāl in 'al-Ḥamd') and the principle of equality; otherwise there is no contradiction.
This illustrates the importance of reconciling textual evidences in Islamic legal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَلَا تُطْلَبُ عَلَى الثَّالِثِ كلبس النعل.
(قوله: وَاسْتُشْكِلَ... إلخ) يحتمل أن نائب فاعله ضمير يعود على العمل بالخبرين السابقين وأنه الجار والمجرور.
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي .
لعارض؛ لأن العارِضَ إنما يتسبب عنه مَنْعُ الاستعمال فقط، ولا يمنع التسمية؛ إذ المحل في ذاته قابل لها، فلا مراغَمَةَ. كذا في حواشي البهجة" نقلاً عن "العباب" وغيره.
عنه لذاته،
وأخذ من هذا بعض المحققين من أشياخنا أنه لو عَرَضَ الإباحةُ لما نُهِيَ كأن اضطر لأكل الميتة أو شُرْبِ جَرْعَةِ حَمرٍ لإساعة ما غَصَّ به مَنْ يريد الأَدَم سِوَى البصل النيء؛ تَبْقَى التسمية على الامتناع؛ إذ المحل في ذاته غيرُ قابِل لها، والضرورة لا مَدْخَلَ لها في التسمية. فتدبر. (قوله: وَلَا تُطْلَبُ عَلَى الثَّالِثِ أي بل الأولى في مثل ذلك: تَرْكُها تعظيماً لاسمه تعالى، وقد يستحبُّ تركُ الذِكْرِ ولو لم يكن ثَمَّ منافٍ للتعظيم ، فقد كَرِهَ الإمام مالك التلبية في غير أيام الحج، فلا تكون البسملةُ مُبَاحَةً أصلاً كما أفاده الصَّبانُ، وللأمير في بدء "شرح المجموع" وحاشيته "ضوء الشموع " كلامٌ في ذلك. فليراجع.
(قوله: وَأَنْ لَا يَجْعَلَ لَهُ الشَّارِعُ مَبْدَأ... إلخ) صادِقٌ بصورتين: ما إذا لم يَجْعَلْ له مبدأ أصلاً، أو جَعَلَ مبدأه البسملة، والصورة الأولى غيرُ مُرَادَة؛ لأنها لا تُوجَدُ إلا في المحرَّم لذاته، أو المكروه لذاته، أو الذِّكْر المَحْضِ، أو سَفَاسِفِ الأمور، وقد أُخْرِجَ ما ذُكِرَ بما تقدم. (قوله: بَيْنَهُمَا تَعَارُضٌ أي على رواية رفع دال (الحمد)، وعلى التساوي، وإلا؛ فقد قيل بعدمه.)
(His saying: 'And it is not sought upon the third type' – like wearing sandals.
His saying: 'And it is objected... etc.' – it is possible that the agent of the passive verb is a pronoun referring to acting upon the two preceding reports (al-khabarayn), and that the prepositional phrase (al-jār wa al-majrūr) is the predicate.
Notes of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi.
For circumstance; because circumstance only brings about prevention of usage and does not prevent saying basmalah, since the locus in its essence is receptive to it, so there is no defiance. Thus in the glosses of 'al-Bahjah' quoting from 'al-‘Ubāb' and others.
Concerning it by essence,
And some verifying scholars among our shaykhs derived from this that if permissibility were to occur for that which is prohibited – such as being forced to eat carrion or drink a gulp of wine to quench choking except for raw onion – the basmalah remains prohibited; because the locus in its essence is not receptive to it, and necessity has no entry in basmalah. So reflect.
(His saying: 'And it is not sought upon the third type' – i.e., rather the better is to leave it out of reverence for His name, Exalted. And it may be recommended to leave remembrance even if there is no conflict with reverence; indeed Imam Malik disliked talbiyah outside the days of Hajj. So basmalah is not absolutely permissible as al-Ṣabbān indicated. And al-Amīr has discussion on this at the beginning of 'Sharḥ al-Majmū‘' and its gloss 'Ḍaw' al-Shumū‘'. So let it be consulted.
(His saying: 'And that the Lawgiver does not make for it a beginning... etc.') It applies to two cases: either He did not make a beginning at all, or He made its beginning the basmalah. The first case is not intended, because it occurs only in things prohibited by essence, disliked by essence, pure dhikr, or trivial matters. And what was mentioned has been excluded by what preceded.
(His saying: 'Between them there is an apparent contradiction' – i.e., according to the narration with raf‘ of the dāl of 'al-Ḥamd', and according to equality (al-tasāwī); otherwise it has been said there is no contradiction.)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage covers the conditions for the basmalah to be recommended (mustaḥabb) or 'sought' (maṭlūb) before an act, and addresses an objection regarding two apparently contradictory reports. The author first states that basmalah is not sought upon the 'third type'—glossed as acts like wearing sandals (i.e., acts that are neither clearly recommended nor prohibited/disliked in essence, but are such that saying basmalah upon them is not prescribed; rather, it is better to leave it out of reverence). He then mentions an objection: it is objected that the two reports (khabarayn) about basmalah for prayer seem contradictory, so how can one act upon both? The glossator notes that the agent of 'is objected' may be a pronoun referring to acting upon the two reports, and the prepositional phrase may be the predicate. Then, after some interpolated text from the previous lesson (about circumstance), the author returns to the condition: 'And that the Lawgiver does not make for it a beginning other than basmalah and ḥamdalah' – meaning if the Lawgiver has prescribed a different opening for an act (like takbīr for prayer), then basmalah is not sought before it. This condition covers two scenarios: (1) the Lawgiver prescribed no beginning at all, (2) the Lawgiver prescribed the basmalah itself as the beginning. The first scenario is not intended because it only occurs in cases of acts prohibited by essence, disliked by essence, pure dhikr, or trivial matters—all of which have already been excluded by preceding conditions. Finally, the objection is addressed: the apparent contradiction between the two reports (one showing basmalah is prescribed for prayer, the other showing it is not) is reconciled by considering the different narrations (one with raf‘ of the dāl of 'al-Ḥamd') and the principle of equality; otherwise it has been said there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
الثالث
مبدأ
الخبران
تعارض
التسمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think basmalah is always recommended before any act.
Correction: The passage specifies that basmalah is not sought for acts that have a prescribed beginning (like prayer with takbir) or that fall under the 'third type' (acts like wearing sandals).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on saying basmalah before an act for which the Lawgiver has prescribed a specific beginning other than basmalah, such as prayer?
A) It is recommended.
B) It is not sought (lā tuṭlab).
C) It is prohibited.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Basmalah is recommended only when the act has no prescribed opening from the Lawgiver and is not from the third type; apparent contradictions in reports are resolved through careful textual analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever said 'Bismillah' before an act that you knew was questionable, hoping it would make it acceptable? After learning that the locus of such an act may not be receptive to basmalah, how will you now examine your intentions and actions before uttering God's name?
?
The scholars recommend omitting basmalah out of reverence for acts of the third type. Is there a religious phrase you use routinely without considering the context or the reverence due to Allah's name? Will you commit to being more mindful of when and where you say 'Bismillah'?
?
When you encounter two seemingly contradictory hadith, do you feel inclined to dismiss one or pick the easier interpretation? This lesson shows that scholars resolve such contradictions through careful analysis. How will you change your approach to hadith that appear to conflict, so that you submit to the full weight of revelation rather than your own preference?

The Evidence for Combining Salat and Salam
Al-Bajuri cites hadith and Quran to justify combining salat and salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence (hadith and Quran) that encourages combining salat and salam when mentioning the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Quran commands both salat and salam together.

In this passage, al-Bajuri explains why the author combined salat and salam. He first cites a hadith about the reward for writing salat in a book, then the Quranic verse that commands both salat and salam. The apparent meaning is that combining them is requested.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith evidence
Notice the hadith: whoever sends salat upon the Prophet in writing will have angels seeking forgiveness for them as long as the Prophet's name remains. This establishes the virtue of salat.
The hadith is the primary motivation for mentioning salat.
2
Reflect on the Quranic command
Read the verse from Surah al-Ahzab (33:56) which commands both salat and salam. The phrase 'with full submission' implies combining them.
The verse is a direct address to believers.
3
Understand the implication
The apparent meaning of the verse is a request to combine both. This sets the stage for the ruling discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنما أتى بالصلاة عليه الله لخبر: «مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيَّ فِي كِتَابٍ؛ لَمْ تَزَلِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ تَسْتَغْفِرُ لَهُ مَا دَامَ اسْمِي فِي ذَلِكَ الْكِتَابِ)، وإنما أتي معها بالسلام لقوله تعالى: يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا ) (٢)، فإن الظاهر منه: طَلَبُ الجمع بينهما، ولذلك كُرة إفرادُ الصَّلاة عن السّلام وعَكْسُه عند المتأخرين، وأما عند المتقدمين؛ فهو خلافُ الأولى فقط كما صَرَّحَ به ابنُ الجَوْزِيّ حيث قال: إن الجمع بين الصلاة والسلام هو الأولى، ولو اقتصر على أحدهما؛ جاز من غير كراهة، فقد جرى على ذلك جماعة من السلف والخلف منهم الإمام مسلم في أول صحيحه) والإمام أبو القاسم الشاطبي. اهـ.
[The author] only brought salat upon him (peace be upon him) because of the report: 'Whoever sends salat upon me in a book, the angels continue to seek forgiveness for him as long as my name is in that book.' And he brought salam with it because of His statement: 'O you who have believed, send salat upon him and salam with full submission' (33:56). The apparent meaning of this is the request to combine both. Therefore, later scholars disliked separating salat from salam or vice versa. As for earlier scholars, it is merely contrary to what is preferable, as Ibn al-Jawzi stated: 'Combining salat and salam is preferable, and if one restricts himself to one of them, it is permissible without dislike.' Many of the salaf and khalaf acted upon this, including Imam Muslim at the beginning of his Sahih and Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Shatibi.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a proof and ruling regarding sending salawat and salam. Al-Bajuri explains why the author (Sanusi) mentioned both salat and salam together. First, the hadith motivates sending salat upon the Prophet in writing, promising forgiveness. Second, the Quranic verse (33:56) commands both salat and salam, and the apparent meaning is to combine them. Consequently, later scholars considered it disliked (makruh) to mention only one, but earlier scholars considered it merely contrary to preference (khilaf al-ula), not disliked. Al-Bajuri cites Ibn al-Jawzi to support the earlier view and names examples from the salaf. The passage thus clarifies the difference of opinion and the basis for each.

Key Terms
الصلاة
السلام
الجمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think sending salat alone is sufficient when mentioning the Prophet.
Correction: The Quran commands both salat and salam, implying that combining them is recommended.

Checkpoint
What does the Quranic verse command believers to do regarding the Prophet?
A) Send salat only
B) Send salam only
C) Send both salat and salam
D) Send salat sometimes and salam other times

Key Takeaway
The primary evidence for combining salat and salam is the Quranic command in verse 33:56.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you write or say the Prophet's name, do you consciously combine salat and salam, or do you often omit one? What does your habit reveal about your reverence for him? Will you commit to always saying 'sallallahu alayhi wa sallam' from now on?
?
The hadith promises angelic forgiveness for those who send salat. But the Quran commands both salat and salam. Are you willing to sacrifice that forgiveness by neglecting the command? How will you ensure you never separate them again?
?
The verse says 'salam with full submission.' Is your salam a mere formality, or does it reflect a heart fully submitted to following the Prophet's sunnah? What one change will you make today to turn your words into sincere devotion?

The Ruling on Combining or Separating Salat and Salam
Al-Bajuri explains the ruling difference between later and earlier scholars regarding separating salat and salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between later scholars (who deemed separation disliked) and earlier scholars (who considered it merely contrary to preference).

Core Idea
Earlier scholars allowed separation without dislike, later scholars discouraged it.

Al-Bajuri now explains the ruling derived from the evidence. He notes that later scholars disliked separating salat from salam, while earlier scholars considered it merely contrary to preference. This distinction is important for understanding the legal flexibility in this matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the text to find the ruling of later scholars (disliked) and earlier scholars (contrary to preference). Notice the different terminology: 'makruh' vs. 'khilaf al-ula'.
2
Understand the earlier scholars' view
Focus on the quote from Ibn al-Jawzi: combining is preferable, but one may limit to one without dislike. This shows the earlier position.
Ibn al-Jawzi is a prominent Hanbali scholar.
3
Note the examples
Al-Bajuri mentions Imam Muslim and Imam al-Shatibi as examples of earlier scholars who acted on this permissibility. Reflect on why their practice matters.
These are respected authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[The author] only brought salat upon him (peace be upon him) because of the report: 'Whoever sends salat upon me in a book, the angels continue to seek forgiveness for him as long as my name is in that book.' And he brought salam with it because of His statement: 'O you who have believed, send salat upon him and salam with full submission' (33:56). The apparent meaning of this is the request to combine both. Therefore, later scholars disliked separating salat from salam or vice versa. As for earlier scholars, it is merely contrary to what is preferable, as Ibn al-Jawzi stated: 'Combining salat and salam is preferable, and if one restricts himself to one of them, it is permissible without dislike.' Many of the salaf and khalaf acted upon this, including Imam Muslim at the beginning of his Sahih and Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Shatibi.

Commentary
This passage is a proof and ruling regarding sending salawat and salam. Al-Bajuri explains why the author (Sanusi) mentioned both salat and salam together. First, the hadith motivates sending salat upon the Prophet in writing, promising forgiveness. Second, the Quranic verse (33:56) commands both salat and salam, and the apparent meaning is to combine them. Consequently, later scholars considered it disliked (makruh) to mention only one, but earlier scholars considered it merely contrary to preference (khilaf al-ula), not disliked. ?

?
The earlier scholars allowed separation ‘without dislike’—do you sometimes impose stricter standards on yourself or others than what is actually required, risking unnecessary hardship? How can you apply the principle of khilaf al-ula to make your practice of Islam more balanced?

The Prophet's Benefit from Salawat
Argument for the Prophet's benefit from salawat with refutation of an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet benefits from prayers despite having been given all perfection, and how the argument from continuous progression supports this.

Core Idea
The Prophet never stops progressing in perfection, so prayers bring him benefit.

This lesson examines a subtle theological point: do the prayers (salawat) of the Ummah benefit the Prophet himself? Some argued that since he has already received all perfection, prayers only benefit the one who prays. However, the correct view is that the Prophet continues to advance in perfection, and each prayer can contribute to that advancement. We'll explore the proof from the Qur'an and the commentary's refinements.

Guided Path
1
State the correct view
Read the beginning of the passage that declares the correct view: the Prophet benefits from salawat like other prophets. Note that this is the established position.
2
Understand the objection
Identify the objection: that benefit only returns to the one praying because perfection has been poured upon the Prophet. This challenges the correct view.
The objectors argue that the Prophet is complete at death, so no benefit can reach him.
3
Examine the refutation
The refutation uses the idea of continuous progression: the Prophet keeps ascending in perfections forever, as each moment is better than the previous, misinterpretations of the verse 'And the Hereafter is better for you than the first.'
This argument shows that even after death, the Prophet can receive additional perfection from our prayers.
4
Apply the nuance
Notice the commentator's additional points: this benefit is before and after death, but it is not appropriate to explicitly state it. Reflect on why such discretion might be advised.
The passage ends with a caution that though correct, one should not publicly declare this benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصحيح أنه ينتفع بالصلاة عليه كغيره من باقي الأنبياء. وقيل: المنفعة عائدة على المصلى ليس إلا لأنه قد أُفُرغَتْ عليه الكمالات. ورد: بأنه لا يزال يترقى في الكمالات دائماً وأبداً؛ إذ ما من كمال إلا وعند الله أَكْمَلُ منه كما أُشِيرَ لذلك بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَلآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنَ الْأُولَى﴾ بناء على ما قاله أهلُ الحقيقة من أن المعنى ولَلَّحْظَةُ المتأخرة خير لك من اللحظة المتقدمة، لكن لا ينبغي التصريح بذلك، وقد أشار بعضهم لذلك بقوله: وَصَحْحُوا بِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَفِعُ بِذِي الصَّلَاةِ شَأْنُهُ مُرْتَفِعُ. لَكِنَّهُ لَا يَنْبَغِي التَّصْرِيحُ لَنَا بِذَا الْقَوْلِ وَذَا صَحِيحُ. (قوله: كَغَيْرِهِ مِنْ بَاقِي الْأَنْبِيَاءِ أي فإن الصحيح أنهم ينتفعون بصلاتنا عليهم، فالخلاف جارٍ فيهم أيضاً كما تُصَرِّحُ به عبارة الشَّرْقَاوِي على الهُدْهُدِي، خلافاً لما يُوهِمُهُ ظاهر المحشي والظاهرُ: أن هذا الخلاف إنما هو بعد الوفاة، أما قَبْلَها؛ فالظاهرُ أنه ينتفِعُ قولاً واحداً أخذاً من التعليل. (قوله: لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ أُفَرغَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْكَمَالَاتُ أي: حين خروجه من الدنيا، وأما قبل ذلك؛ فكان يترقى في الكمالات تأمل. (قوله: بِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَفِعُ) لعل الباء زائدة، أو ضَمَّنَ (صححوا) معنى تمشكوا مثلاً.
And the correct view is that he (the Prophet) benefits from prayer upon him, like other prophets. And it was said: the benefit returns only to the one praying, because perfection has been poured upon him. And it was refuted by [saying] that he continues to progress in perfections forever and always; for there is no perfection except that with Allah there is something more perfect than it, as was alluded to in His words: 'And the Hereafter is better for you than the first [life]' (93:4), based on what the people of reality said: that the meaning is 'the later moment is better for you than the earlier moment,' but it is not appropriate for us to explicitly state that, and some alluded to that by saying: 'And they corrected that he benefits by this prayer – his status is elevated.' But it is not appropriate for us to explicitly state this saying, and this is correct. (His words: 'like other prophets' means that the correct view is that they benefit from our prayers upon them, so the disagreement also applies to them, as the expression of al-Sharqāwī on al-Hudhudī makes clear, contrary to what the apparent meaning of the commentator (muḥashshī) suggests. And the apparent [view] is that this disagreement is only after death; before it, the apparent [view] is that he benefits, unanimously, taken from the justification. (His words: 'because perfection has been poured upon him' means: at the time of his departure from this world; before that, he would progress in perfections, reflect. (His words: 'that he benefits') – perhaps the bā' is extra, or he (the author of the matn) included in 'ṣaḥḥaḥū' the meaning of 'they held firmly' for example.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents and defends the opinion that the Prophet (and other prophets) benefit from the prayers (salawat) of the Ummah. It begins by stating the correct view: the Prophet benefits from salawat, just like other prophets. Then an objection is raised: the benefit of the prayer only returns to the one who prays, because the Prophet has already been given complete perfection. This is refuted by the argument that the Prophet continually increases in perfection indefinitely, since for every perfection there is a greater one with Allah, as indicated by the verse 'And the Hereafter is better for you than the first [life]', interpreted by the gnostics to mean each later moment is better than the previous one. Therefore, the prayer can contribute to his ongoing increase. The commentator then adds that it is inappropriate to explicitly state this benefit, although it is correct. He then comments on matn phrases: 'like other prophets'—the disagreement about benefit applies to all prophets, but before death they benefit unanimously; 'because perfection has been poured upon him'—this refers to the time of death, not before; and 'that he benefits'—the bā' in 'bihi' may be extra, or the verb implies holding firmly. The passage ends with the matn's statement that explicit declaration is not appropriate and that this is correct.

Key Terms
الصلاة
الانتفاع
الكمالات
ترقى
المصلى
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets do not benefit from prayers because they are already perfect and lack nothing.
Correction: The passage proves they benefit because they continue to progress in perfection indefinitely, so prayers can add to their rank.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof that the Prophet continues to benefit from salawat?
A) The Prophet's perfection was complete at death.
B) The verse about the Hereafter being better than the first life, implying continuous progression.
C) The unanimous agreement of scholars.
D) The fact that the bā' is extra.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet benefits from salawat because he perpetually increases in perfection, and each prayer contributes to that increase.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every moment of your life is an opportunity to raise the rank of the Prophet through salawat, how many authentic, heartfelt prayers have you sent today? What is stopping you from making this a constant practice?
?
The verse 'لَلآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنَ الْأُولَى' is interpreted as each later moment being better than the last. Is your own spiritual state improving moment by moment, or are you stagnating? What will you change starting now?
?
Do you truly believe that your small, careless salawat can add to the Prophet's perfection? If so, why do you often rush through them? If not, what does that say about your faith in the power of this act of worship?

The Meaning of 'Salam' for the Prophet
Exegesis of the meaning of 'salam' in the blessing formula.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various interpretations of 'salam' in the context of invoking blessings upon the Prophet and the reasons some interpretations are preferred.

Core Idea
The greeting 'salam' holds multiple layers: safety, greeting, and a divine attribute.

This passage delves into the rich meaning of 'salam' when we say 'upon him be peace'. It examines several scholarly interpretations, from safety for the Prophet and his community to a divine greeting. The commentator also warns against taking it as the divine name in this context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'salam'
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully, noting the different interpretations presented.
Pay attention to the commentator's evaluation of each interpretation.
2
Identify the interpretations
List each interpretation of 'salam' mentioned: safety from fear for Ummah, safety on Day of Judgment, as greeting (tahiyya), and the rejected interpretation as divine name.
There are four main interpretations.
3
Understand the commentator's judgment
Note which interpretations are accepted and which are rejected as far-fetched.
The commentator does not deny the divine name, but rejects its application here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا ما يتعلق بالصلاة. وأما السلام فمعناه الأمان، والمراد: تأمينه مما يخاف على أمته؛ لأنه الله معصوم، فكيف يخاف على نفسه؟ نعم يخاف على نفسه خَوْفَ مهابة وإجلال؛ إذ المرء كلما اشتدَّ قُرْبُه من الله؛ اشتدَّ خَوْفُه منه، ولذلك قال : «إِنِّي لَأَخْوَفُكُمْ مِنَ الله». وقيل: المراد : تأمينه الله مما يخاف على نفسه عند اشتداد الكَرْب في المحشر ؛ لأنه يَنْسَى العصمة كسائر الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وفَسَّرَهُ بعضهم بالتحية والمراد بها في حقه تعالى مع رُسُله: أنه يخاطبه بكلامه القديم دالاً على رِفْعَة مقامه العظيم. وتوهَّمَ بعضهم أن المراد بالسلام هنا: اسمه تعالى قال: والمعنى الله راض، أو حفيظ على رسوله. ولا يخفى ما فيه من البُعْدِ. وبالجملة لا تُنكِرُ ثبوت السّلام اسماً من أسمائه تعالى، ولكن يَبْعُدُ حَمْلُه عليه في مثل هذا الموضع. وبَقِيَتْ أبحاث تتعلق بالصلاة والسّلام لا تناسب هنا. (قوله: عَلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ) متعلّق بمحذوف تقديره : كائنان، وهو خبر عن قوله: (والصلاة والسلام والمراد برسول الله هنا خصوص سيدنا محمد ، لا كلُّ رسول كما حمله على ذلك بعضُهم؛ لأن ذلك اللفظَ غَلَبَ استعماله في نبينا محمد صار لا يُطْلَقُ على غيره إلا مقروناً بذكره أو قرينة.
This concerns the prayer (ṣalāh). As for the greeting (salām), its meaning is safety/security (amān). The intended meaning is: securing him from what he fears for his nation, because he is protected by Allāh (ma‘ṣūm), so how could he fear for himself? Yes, he fears for himself [with] the fear of awe and veneration; for whenever a person draws closer to Allāh, his fear of Him intensifies. That is why he said: 'I am the most fearful of you of Allāh.' And it was said: the intended meaning is Allāh's securing him from what he fears for himself at the time of intense distress in the gathering (of judgment), because he forgets his infallibility (ʿiṣma) like other prophets, peace and prayers be upon them. And some interpreted it as greeting (taḥiyya), and what is meant by it concerning Him, Exalted, with His messengers is: that He addresses him with His eternal speech, indicating the loftiness of his great station. And some falsely imagined that the intended meaning here of 'salām' is His name, Exalted, and they said: the meaning is 'Allāh is pleased' or 'Allāh is guardian over His messenger.' And it is not hidden what [distance/far-fetchedness] is in that. In summary, we do not deny the affirmation of 'salām' as one of His names, Exalted, but it is far-fetched to apply it here in such a context. And there remain investigations concerning the prayer and greeting that are not suitable here. (His words: 'upon the Messenger of Allāh') – it is attached to an omitted element whose estimation is 'existing both' (kā'inān), and it is the predicate of his words 'the prayer and the greeting.' And what is meant by 'Messenger of Allāh' here is specifically our master Muḥammad, not every messenger, as some have taken it; because that expression has become predominantly used for our Prophet Muḥammad, such that it is not applied to others except accompanied by his mention or a contextual indicator.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage forms a commentary on the meaning of 'salam' (greeting/peace) and the phrase 'upon the Messenger of Allah'. It begins by concluding the discussion of prayer (salah) and transitions to 'salam', stating its core meaning: safety/security (aman). The commentator then explores possible interpretations. First, salam means granting the Prophet security from what he fears for his Ummah, noting that while the Prophet is protected by Allah and should not fear for himself in an ordinary sense, he does experience fear out of awe and reverence—the closer one is to Allah, the greater the fear. A second interpretation is that Allāh grants the Prophet security from his own fear on the Day of Judgment when he forgets his infallibility like other prophets. A third interpretation by some scholars is that 'salam' here means 'greeting' (tahiyya), which for Allah means addressing the Prophet with His eternal speech. Another group mistakenly thought 'salam' refers to the divine name 'as-Salam', meaning Allah is pleased or guardian, but the commentator rejects this as far-fetched, though he does not deny that 'Salam' is a divine name. Finally, the commentator addresses the phrase 'upon the Messenger of Allah', noting it specifically refers to Prophet Muhammad, because the term 'Rasul Allah' has become predominantly used for him and is not applied to other prophets except with a qualifying mention.

Key Terms
السلام
الأمان
المهابة
العصمة
التحية
اسم الله السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that 'salam' in this context is the divine name 'as-Salam', meaning Allah is pleased or guardian.
Correction: The commentator rejects this as far-fetched (bā‘id), though he does not deny that 'as-Salam' is a divine name.

Checkpoint
What is the commentator's view on interpreting 'salam' as the divine name in this context?
A) He strongly rejects it as impossible.
B) He considers it far-fetched but does not deny the name itself.
C) He accepts it without qualification.
D) He says it is the only correct interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The word 'salam' in blessings upon the Prophet has multiple valid interpretations, but it should not be taken as the divine name in this context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam', do you ponder the depth of 'salām' and your own need for security from Allah's wrath, or is it a mere habit? What would change if you truly believed that each 'sallam' carries a plea for safety on the Day of Judgment?
?
The Prophet, despite his infallibility, feared Allah with the utmost awe. How does your heart respond to this? Are you content to follow a religion without fear, or do you sense the urgency to intensify your own reverence and accountability before Allah?
?
The commentator rejects interpreting 'salām' as the divine name in this context, warning against forcing meanings that do not fit. Where in your own understanding of Islam might you be imposing meanings that suit your desires rather than the intended message? Ask Allah to guide you to the correct understanding.

Why 'Rasul Allah' Specifically Refers to Muhammad
Clarification of the referent of 'Rasul Allah' in the blessing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic principle that the term 'Rasul Allah' predominantly refers to Prophet Muhammad and is not generalized to all messengers.

Core Idea
Context and customary usage make 'Rasul Allah' uniquely refer to Prophet Muhammad.

In the blessing formula, the phrase 'the Messenger of Allah' is used. This lesson explains why it specifically denotes Prophet Muhammad and not any other messenger, based on the predominant usage of the term.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'Rasul Allah'
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the phrase 'upon the Messenger of Allah' and the commentator's explanation.
2
Identify the claim
The commentator states that 'Rasul Allah' here specifically refers to our master Muhammad, not every messenger.
3
Understand the reason
The reason given is that the expression has become overwhelmingly (għalaba) used for Muhammad, so it is not applied to others without qualification.
This is a linguistic principle of predominant usage (ghalabat al-isti‘māl).

The Two Senses of Legal Judgment
Al-Anbabi resolves a contradiction by distinguishing two senses of legal judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that legal judgment (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī) has two distinct meanings: as an act of stipulation by the Lawgiver and as the eternal speech of Allah.

Core Idea
Legal judgment is both a divine act and divine speech—two sides of one reality.

Al-Anbābī, a later commentator, clarifies a seeming inconsistency in the earlier text. When the author spoke of 'legal judgment' in different ways, he was referring to two different aspects of the same concept. This distinction helps avoid confusion and deepens our understanding of Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the structure: a contradiction is raised, then resolved by a two-part definition.
2
Identify the two senses
The passage explicitly lists two 'iṭlāqayn' (senses). Find them: first, judgment as the act of affirming or negating by a stipulator; second, as the speech of Allah. Note that the second is left partial in the text.
3
Understand the resolution
The apparent contradiction arose because the author used 'legal judgment' in both senses. Al-Anbābī resolves it by showing they are two different levels or aspects, not conflicting definitions.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters in Uṣūl al-Fiqh and Kalām. It shows that divine rulings have both a conceptual existence (in divine will) and a verbal expression (in revelation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي المتعلّق... إلخ، ففي كلامه تناف. ويجاب عن ذلك بأن للحكم الشرعي إطلاقين: الأول: إثباتُ أمرٍ لأمرٍ أو نَفْيُهُ عنه بواسطة وضع الواضع، وهذا هو ما أشار إليه أولاً، الثاني: كلام الله المتعلق... إلخ، وهو ما أشار إليه ثانياً.
The notes of al-ʿAllāma Muḥammad al-Anbābī: 'The related... etc.' So in his speech there is contradiction. And it is answered that legal judgment has two senses: the first: the affirmation of a thing for a thing or its negation from it by means of the stipulation of a stipulator, and this is what he indicated first; the second: the speech of Allah related... etc., and this is what he indicated second.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage resolves an apparent contradiction in the author's statements about legal judgment. Al-Anbābī explains that legal judgment (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī) has two meanings. First, it can mean a judgment made by a lawgiver (al-wāḍiʿ) – i.e., Allah – who stipulates that something is required, prohibited, etc. This is the judgment considered as an act of establishing a rule. Second, it can mean the actual speech of Allah (kalām Allāh) that contains the ruling. The author referred to both, which might seem contradictory, but they are two different aspects of the same reality.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-ḥukm al-sharʿī)
وضع الواضع (waḍʿ al-wāḍiʿ)
كلام الله (kalām Allāh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That legal judgment is only one thing without distinction.
Correction: Legal judgment has two valid senses: the act of stipulation by Allah and the speech of Allah. Both are used in scholarly discourse, and recognizing this resolves apparent contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to al-Anbābī, what are the two senses of legal judgment?
A) Rational and customary.
B) As judgment by stipulation and as the speech of Allah.
C) As affirmative and negative.
D) As necessary and possible.

Key Takeaway
Legal judgment refers both to Allah's act of stipulating a rule and to His speech that expresses that rule.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse from the Quran that commands or prohibits, do you see it only as a rule to follow, or do you also see it as the very speech of Allah addressing you personally? Which perspective will you intentionally adopt today?
?
Think of a ruling of Islam that you find difficult to obey. Does thinking of it as a divine act (a ruling decreed by Allah) or as divine speech (Allah’s personal word to you) change how you approach it? How will you remind yourself of both aspects?
?
The lesson distinguishes between the act of stipulation and the speech itself. In your daily life, do you treat the Quranic commands more as dry legal obligations or as the living word of your Creator? What step will you take tonight to bridge the gap between knowing the ruling and hearing Allah speak through it?

The Sufficiency of a Prophet's Call: Two Views
Sanusi states the two views on the sufficiency of a prophet's call and the saved status of ahl al-fatrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two views on whether any prophet's call suffices for accountability and the status of ahl al-fatrah according to the correct view.

Core Idea
No binding obligation without a personal prophet's call.

Sanusi presents a key debate: is it enough to receive the message of any prophet, or must it be the specific prophet sent to one's people? The correct view is the latter, which has important implications for those who lived in intervals between prophets (ahl al-fatrah). In this passage, he explains that they are saved even if they committed idolatry, because the call never reached them in a binding way.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two opinions presented at the start.
The passage begins with 'واختلف' indicating a point of disagreement.
2
Identify the two views
The first view: any prophet's call suffices. The second: only the call of the prophet sent to that person suffices. The correct view is the second.
The phrase 'والصحيحُ الثاني' establishes the preferred position.
3
Understand the implication for ahl al-fatrah
Since the correct view requires the specific prophet's call, people in intervals (ahl al-fatrah) are saved because no such call reached them. Even if they worshipped idols, they are not punished.
The text says 'فأهلُ الفترة ناجون' despite their idolatry.
4
Consider the exceptions
Some individuals like Imru' al-Qais and Hatim al-Ta'i are excepted because Allah knew they would have opposed the Prophet. This shows that knowledge of their character can override the general rule.
This nuance is found in the commentary.
5
Review the summary of positions
The 'حاصل ما يقال' part summarizes the positions of Maturidis, Mu'tazila, and al-Nawawi. For those not reached, only some Maturidis and Mu'tazila punish them. For those reached, all groups punish them. Those who attain tawhid are saved according to each school's criteria.
This shows how the two views interact with different theological foundations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف هل يُكْتَفَى بدعوة أي رسول كان ولو آدَمَ أو لا بُدَّ من دعوة الرسول الذي أُرْسِلَ إلى هذا الشخص والصحيحُ الثاني وعليه فأهلُ الفَتْرَة ناجون؛ وإن غَيَّروا وبدلوا وعبدوا الأوثانَ.
(قوله: بِدَعْوَةِ أَي رَسُولٍ) أي: دعاءه الناس إلى معرفة ما يتعلق بالله ورسوله. (قوله: فَأَهْلُ الْفَتْرَةِ نَاجُونَ إلا من ورد النص بتعذيبهم كامرئ القيس وحاتم الطائي لمعنى عَلِمَهُ الله فيهم بأن علم أنهم لو أدركوا النبي لعاندوا.
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي .
(قوله: وَعَلَيْهِ فَأَهْلُ الْفَتْرَةِ هي - بفتح الفاء وسكون المثناة ـ ما بين النبتين، من: الفُتُور وهي الغفلةُ والتَّرْكُ؛ لأنهم تُرِكُوا بلا ،رسول، فالعرب القدماء الذين أدركوا عيسى من أهل الفترة على الصحيح؛ لأنه لم يُرْسَلْ لهم، وإنما أُرْسِلَ لبني إسرائيل، والعرب لم يُرْسَلْ إليهم إلا سيدنا إسماعيل ونبينا الذي هو من ذرّيَّته وعلى بقية النبيين، فجميع العرب صاروا أهلَ فترةٍ بموت سيدنا إسماعيل إلى بعثة نبينا .
وأما على القول بأن المدارَ على بلوغ دَعْوَةِ أي نبي كان؛ فليسوا أهل فترةٍ، فهم في النار إن بَدَّلوا. وهذا القولُ هو الذي ذهب إليه النَّوَوِيُّ ووُجّه بأن التوحيد ليس أمراً خاصاً بهذه الأمة، لكنه ضعيف.
وحاصل ما يقال: إن الذي لم تَبْلُغه دعوة لا يقول بتعذيبه إلا بعض المَاتُرِيدِيَّةِ والمعتزلة؛ لبناء أمر المعرفة على العقل عند الفريقين، وأما الذي بَلَغَتْهُ الدعوة، فغَيَّرَ أو قَصَّرَ، فكَفَرَ؛ فيقول بتعذيبه مَنْ ذُكِرَ من الفريقين، والنووي ومن معه، فمتى حَصَلَتِ المعرفة والتوحيد لشخص من أهل الفترة؛ نَجَا باتفاق عند من قال بكفاية العقل لقيامه بالواجب، وَعِنْدَ من قال بالشرع واكتفى بدعوة رسول ما لقيامه بالواجب أيضاً إن كان سَمِعَها، وإلا؛ فلعدم وجوبها عليه وَعِنْدَ مَنْ قال بالشرع بشرط أن يكون مُرْسَلاً إليه لعدم وجوبها عليه، سواءٌ سَمِعَ من رسول لم يُرْسَلْ إليه أو لم يسمع، وتبرُّعُه بها لا يضرُّهُ.
And there is disagreement: Is it sufficient (to be accountable) by the call of any messenger, even Adam, or must it be the call of the messenger who was sent to this person? The correct (view) is the second, and accordingly the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) are saved, even if they changed, altered, and worshipped idols.
(His saying: 'by the call of any messenger') i.e., his calling people to knowledge of what pertains to God and His messenger. (His saying: 'so the people of the interval are saved') except those for whom scriptural evidence of punishment came, like Imru' al-Qais and Hatim al-Ta'i, for a meaning that God knew in them, namely that He knew that if they had encountered the Prophet they would have opposed him.
Annotations of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi:
(His saying: 'and accordingly the people of the interval are') – with a fatha on the fa and sukun on the (ta') – the interval between two prophets, from: al-futur, which is heedlessness and abandonment, because they were left without a messenger. The ancient Arabs who encountered Jesus are from the people of the interval according to the correct view, because he was not sent to them; he was only sent to the Children of Israel. The Arabs were sent only our master Ishmael and our Prophet who is from his progeny, and upon the rest of the prophets. So all the Arabs became people of interval from the death of our master Ishmael until the mission of our Prophet.
But according to the view that the criterion is the receipt of the call of any prophet, they are not people of interval, so they are in the Fire if they changed. This is the view that al-Nawawi held, and it was justified by saying that tawhid is not specific to this nation, but it is weak.
The summary of what is said: that the one whom the call has not reached, only some Maturidis and Mu'tazila say he is punished, because the matter of knowledge is based on reason for the two groups. As for the one whom the call reached but changed or fell short, he disbelieves; thus the aforementioned groups and al-Nawawi and those with him say he is punished. Whenever knowledge and tawhid occur for a person from the people of interval, he is saved by agreement according to those who say reason suffices for performing the obligation. And according to those who say (it is based on) revelation and suffice with the call of a certain messenger for performing the obligation, also if he heard it; otherwise, due to its not being obligatory on him. And according to those who say (it is based on) revelation conditioned upon being sent to him, due to its not being obligatory on him, whether he heard from a messenger not sent to him or did not hear; and his voluntarily performing it does not harm him.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents the two opinions on the sufficiency of any prophet's call for accountability. The matn states the correct view is the second: one must have received the call of the specific prophet sent to him. Consequently, ahl al-fatrah (people living in intervals between prophets) are saved, even if they committed idolatry. The commentary clarifies exceptions for those condemned by specific texts. Anbabi's gloss defines 'fatrah' as the interval between two prophets, deriving from 'futur' meaning heedlessness. He gives the example of ancient Arabs who met Jesus: Jesus was sent only to Israel, so those Arabs are from ahl al-fatrah. The Arabs received only Ishmael and Muhammad, so they were in a fatrah from Ishmael to Muhammad. The view of al-Nawawi, that the criterion is receipt of any prophet's call (thus including older messengers), is mentioned but deemed weak. The conclusion explains the positions of the Maturidis, Mu'tazila, and Nawawi: for those who reason suffices, knowledge of tawhid even in a fatrah saves; for those who require revelation, if they heard a messenger's call (any messenger), they are bound; if not, they are not bound. The nuance is that even someone who voluntarily performs tawhid without being bound is not harmed.

Key Terms
أهل الفترة
دعوة
الرسول
التوحيد
المعرفة
العقل
الشرع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-fatrah are automatically saved regardless of any condition.
Correction: They are saved only because the call of a specific prophet did not reach them. However, if they attained knowledge of tawhid through reason or heard another prophet's call, the ruling may differ, and there are exceptions for those condemned by specific texts.

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in this passage, why are ahl al-fatrah saved?
A) Because they used reason alone.
B) Because no prophet's call reached them in a binding way.
C) Because they are not accountable at all.
D) Because they followed any prophet.

Key Takeaway
The saved status of ahl al-fatrah follows from the principle that accountability requires the call of a specific prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have never met a prophet in person, but you have received the call of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Do you truly live as if that call is personally and bindingly addressed to you today, or do you treat it as historical information that doesn't demand your full obedience?
?
This lesson teaches that those who never received a prophetic call are saved. How does that shape your view of people around the world who have not heard Islam? Do you feel a personal urgency to convey the call, knowing that after they hear it, they become accountable?
?
If reason alone does not create binding obligation without a prophet, how do you handle moments when your intellect conflicts with revealed commands? Are you willing to subordinate your logic to the prophetic call, even when it seems difficult or unreasonable?

The Salvation of the Prophet's Parents
Sanusi argues the Prophet's parents are saved, citing ahl al-fatrah and a weak narration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for the salvation of the Prophet's parents according to Sunni theology, including the argument from ahl al-fatrah and the role of the weak hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's parents are saved because they were from ahl al-fatrah; the weak hadith is extra support.

This lesson addresses a question about the fate of the Prophet's parents. The great scholar Sanusi argues they are among the saved, relying on the principle that people who lived during the interval between prophets (ahl al-fatrah) are saved. He also cites a narration that God revived them to believe, but even if that narration is weak, the main argument stands. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand ahl al-fatrah
First, grasp the concept of ahl al-fatrah: people who lived in a period without a prophet. According to Sanusi, they are saved (i.e., not punished for unbelief). This is the foundation of the argument.
2
Apply to the Prophet's parents
Sanusi then applies this: since the Prophet's parents lived before his mission, they are from ahl al-fatrah, and thus saved. He further asserts they are from ahl al-Islam due to a narration.
3
Examine the supporting narration
Read the poetry and gloss. The narration says God revived them after the Prophet's mission so they could believe. The gloss admits the hadith is weak but argues it's not impossible.
4
Understand the gloss's defense
The gloss explains that even if the hadith is weak, it does not contradict reason or revelation, so it can be accepted as evidence. The primary basis, however, is the ahl al-fatrah status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا علمت أن أهل الفترة ناجون؛ عَلِمْتَ أن أبَوَيْه الله ناجيان لكونهما من أهل الفترة، بل هما من أهل الإسلام؛ لما رُوِيَ أن الله تعالى أحياهما بعد بعثة النبي ، فآمنا به، ولذا قال بعضهم:
حبا اللهُ النَّبِيَّ مَزِيدَ فَضْلٍ عَلَى فَضْلٍ وَكَانَ بِهِ رَؤُوفَا
فَأَحْيَا أُمَّهُ وَكَذَا أَبَاهُ لإِيمَانٍ بِهِ فَضْلاً مُنِيفاً
فَسَلَّمَ فَالْقَدِيمُ بِذَا قَدِيرٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْحَدِيثُ بهِ ضَعِيفَا
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: فَضْلاً) متعلق بـ(أحيا)، ومبيناً لمعنى زائد.
(قوله: وَإِنْ كَانَ الْحَدِيثُ بهِ ضَعِيفَا) أي: وإن كان الحديث الوارد في إحيائهما لإيمانهما ضعيفاً، ولكن لا يمنع ذلك من إثبات الإيمان لهما بطريق آخر، لأنه ليس فيه محال عقلي؛ فانعقاده بدليل ولو ظنياً لا عقلاً ولا شرعاً ما يمنعه.
And if you know that the people of the interval are saved, then you know that his (peace be upon him) parents are saved, because they are from the people of the interval; rather, they are from the people of Islam, because it is narrated that God Almighty revived them after the Prophet's mission, and they believed in him. Hence some said:
God gave the Prophet an increase of grace upon grace, and He was kind to him.
So He revived his mother and likewise his father for faith in him, an exalted grace.
So submit: the Eternal is powerful over this, even if the hadith concerning it is weak.
Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhūrī:
(His saying: 'an exalted grace' [faḍlan]) is attached to 'revived' (aḥyā), and it clarifies an additional meaning.
(His saying: 'even if the hadith concerning it is weak') i.e., even if the hadith about their revival for their faith is weak, that does not prevent affirming faith for them by another path, because there is no intellectual impossibility in it; so its establishment by evidence, even if speculative, is prevented neither by reason nor revelation.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage deduces that the Prophet's parents are saved because they belong to ahl al-fatrah. Moreover, some narrations state that God revived them after the Prophet's mission so they could believe in him. The poetry cited emphasizes this as a special grace to the Prophet. The gloss clarifies that even if the hadith about their revival is weak, it is not intellectually impossible; therefore, it can be accepted as evidence, since reason and revelation do not forbid it. The key point is that being from ahl al-fatrah suffices for salvation, and the extra narration merely reinforces it.

Key Terms
أبوا النبي
إحياء
فضل
حديث ضعيف
أهل الفترة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the weak hadith alone is the basis for the salvation of the Prophet's parents.
Correction: The passage shows that the primary basis is their status as ahl al-fatrah; the weak hadith is only supplementary and not essential.

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason given for the salvation of the Prophet's parents?
A) A strong hadith about their revival
B) The fact that they are from ahl al-fatrah
C) Their own independent reasoning
D) The consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's parents are saved because they were from ahl al-fatrah; the weak hadith about their revival is not the primary basis but is permissible as evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you died today without having heard the full message of Islam, what would you expect from God's justice? How does the concept of ahl al-fatrah challenge your assumptions about His mercy?
?
The weak hadith about the Prophet's parents is used as supplementary evidence. Are you willing to accept less-than-certain proofs for matters that bring comfort to your heart? Why or why not?
?
Knowing that the Prophet's parents are saved by God's grace, how does this affect your hope for your own loved ones who died without accepting Islam? Will you let this shape your du'a for them?
